Only used by the SOCKS GSSAPI functions.\\n91:  */\\n92: int Curl_blockread_all(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\\n93:                        struct Curl_easy *data,   /* transfer */\\n94: \\n232: static CURLproxycode socks_state_recv(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\\n233:                                       struct socks_state *sx,\\n234:                                       struct Curl_easy *data,\\n235:                                       CURLproxycode failcode,\\n236:                                       const char *description)\\n237: {\\n238:   ssize_t nread;\\n239:   CURLcode result;\\n240: \\n241:   nread = Curl_conn_cf_recv(cf->next, data, (char *)sx->outp,\\n242:                             sx->outstanding, &result);\\n243:   if(nread <= 0) {\\n244: CURLPX_OK;\\n261: }\\n262: \\n263: /*\\n264: * This function logs in to a SOCKS4 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\\n265: * destination server.\\n266: *\\n267: * Reference :\\n268: *   https://www.openssh.com/txt/socks4.protocol\\n269: *\\n270: * Note :\\n271: *   Set protocol4a=true for  \\\"SOCKS 4A (Simple Extension to SOCKS 4 Protocol)\\\"\\n272: *   Nonsupport \\\"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\\\"\\n273: */\\n274: static CURLproxycode do_SOCKS4(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\\n275:                                struct socks_state *sx,\\n276:                                struct Curl_easy *data)\\n277: {\\n278:   struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\\n279:   const bool protocol4a =\\n280:     (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS4A) ? /* version (SOCKS4) */\\n312:     socksreq[1] = 1; /* connect */\\n313:     socksreq[2] = (unsigned char)((sx->remote_port >> 8) & 0xff); /* MSB */\\n314:     socksreq[3] = (unsigned char)(sx->remote_port & 0xff);        /* LSB */\\n315: \\n316:     /* DNS resolve only for SOCKS4, not SOCKS4a */\\n317:     if(!protocol4a) {\\n318:       enum resolve_t rc =\\n319:         Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port, TRUE, &dns);\\n320: \\n321:       if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\\n322:         return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\\n323:       else if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\\n324:         sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\\n325:         infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4 non-blocking resolve of %s\\\", sx->hostname);\\n326:         return CURLPX_OK;\\n327:       }\\n328:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\\n329:       goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\\n330:     }\\n331: \\n332:     /* socks4a doesn't resolve anything locally */\\n333:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\\n334:     goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\\n335: \\n336:   case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\\n337:     /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\\n338:     dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, (int)conn->port);\\n339: \\n340:     if(dns) {\\n341: #ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\\n342:       data->state.async.dns = dns;\\n343:       data->state.async.done = TRUE;\\n344: #endif\\n345:       infof(data, \\\"Hostname '%s' was found\\\", sx->hostname);\\n346:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\\n347:     }\\n348:     else {\\n349:       result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\\n350:       if(!dns) {\\n351:         if(result)\\n352:           return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\\n353:         return CURLPX_OK;\\n354:       }\\n355:     }\\n356:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n357: CONNECT_RESOLVED:\\n358:   case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\\n359:     struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\\n360:     /*\\n361:      * We cannot use 'hostent' as a struct that Curl_resolv() returns.  It\\n362:      * returns a Curl_addrinfo pointer that may not always look the same.\\n363:      */\\n364:     if(dns) {\\n365:       hp = dns->addr;\\n366: \\n367:       /* scan for the first IPv4 address */\\n368:       while(hp && (hp->ai_family != AF_INET))\\n369:         hp = hp->ai_next;\\n370: \\n371:       if(hp) {\\n372:         struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\\n373:         char buf[64];\\n374:         Curl_printable_address(hp, buf, sizeof(buf));\\n375: \\n376:         saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\\n377:         socksreq[4] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[0];\\n378:         socksreq[5] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[1];\\n379:         socksreq[6] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[2];\\n380:         socksreq[7] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[3];\\n381: \\n382:         infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4 connect to IPv4 %s (locally resolved)\\\", buf);\\n383: \\n384:         Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* ensure empty userid is NUL-terminated */\\n403:     if(sx->proxy_user) {\\n404:       size_t plen = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\\n405:       if(plen >= (size_t)data->set.buffer_size - 8) {\\n406:         failf(data, \\\"Too long SOCKS proxy user name, can't use\\\");\\n407:         return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\\n408:       }\\n409:       /* copy the proxy name WITH trailing zero */\\n410:       memcpy(socksreq + 8, sx->proxy_user, plen + 1);\\n411:     }\\n412: \\n413:     /*\\n414:      * Make connection\\n415:      */\\n416:     {\\n417:       size_t packetsize = 9 +\\n418:         strlen((char *)socksreq + 8); CD is the result\\n483:    * code with one of the following values:\\n484:    *\\n485:    * 90: request granted\\n486:    * 91: request rejected or failed\\n487:    * 92: request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to\\n488:    *     identd on the client\\n489:    * 93: request rejected because the client program and identd\\n490:    *     report different user-ids\\n491:    */\\n492: \\n493:   /* wrong version ? */\\n494:   if(socksreq[0]) {\\n495:     failf(data,\\n496:           \\\"SOCKS4 reply has wrong version, version should be 0.\\\");\\n497:     return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\\n498:   }\\n499: \\n500:   /* Result */\\n501:   switch(socksreq[1]) {\\n502:   case 90:\\n503:     infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4%s request granted.\\\", protocol4a?\\\"a\\\":\\\"\\\");\\n504:     break;\\n505:   case 91:\\n506:     failf(data,\\n507:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n508:           \\\", request rejected or failed.\\\",\\n509:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n510:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n511:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n512:     return CURLPX_REQUEST_FAILED;\\n513:   case 92:\\n514:     failf(data,\\n515:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. Replies\\\". This is what a SOCK5\\n554:     replies:\\n555: \\n556:         +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\\n557:         |VER | REP |  RSV  | ATYP | BND.ADDR | BND.PORT |\\n558:         +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\\n559:         | 1  |  1  | X'00' |  1   | Variable |    2     |\\n560:         +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\\n561: \\n562:     Where:\\n563: \\n564:     o  VER    protocol version: X'05'\\n565:     o  REP    Reply field:\\n566:     o  X'00' succeeded\\n567:   */\\n568:   struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\\n569:   unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\\n570:   int idx;\\n571:   CURLcode result;\\n572:   CURLproxycode presult;\\n573:   bool socks5_resolve_local =\\n574:     (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == CURLPROXY_SOCKS5) ? /* not used anymore from now on */\\n385:       }\\n386:       else\\n387:         failf(data, \\\"SOCKS4 connection to %s not supported\\\", sx->hostname);\\n388:     }\\n389:     else\\n390:       failf(data, \\\"Failed to resolve \\\\\\\"%s\\\\\\\" for SOCKS4 connect.\\\",\\n391:             sx->hostname);\\n392: \\n393:     if(!hp)\\n394:       return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\\n395:   }\\n396:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n397: CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\\n398:   case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\\n399:     /*\\n400:      * This is currently not supporting \\\"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\\\".\\n401:      */\\n402:     socksreq[8] = 0; /* ensure empty userid is NUL-terminated */\\n403:     if(sx->proxy_user) {\\n404:       size_t plen = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\\n405:       if(plen >= (size_t)data->set.buffer_size - 8) {\\n406:         failf(data, \\\"Too long SOCKS proxy user name, can't use\\\");\\n407:         return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\\n408:       }\\n409:       /* copy the proxy name WITH trailing zero */\\n410:       memcpy(socksreq + 8, sx->proxy_user, plen + 1);\\n411:     }\\n412: \\n413:     /*\\n414:      * Make connection\\n415:      */\\n416:     {\\n417:       size_t packetsize = 9 +\\n418:         strlen((char *)socksreq + 8); /* size including NUL */\\n419: \\n420:       /* If SOCKS4a, set special invalid IP address 0.0.0.x */\\n421:       if(protocol4a) {\\n422:         size_t hostnamelen = 0;\\n423:         socksreq[4] = 0;\\n424:         socksreq[5] = 0;\\n425:         socksreq[6] = 0;\\n426:         socksreq[7] = 1;\\n427:         /* append hostname */\\n428:         hostnamelen = strlen(sx->hostname) + 1; /* length including NUL */\\n429:         if(hostnamelen <= 255)\\n430:           strcpy((char *)socksreq + packetsize, sx->hostname);\\n431:         else {\\n432:           failf(data, \\\"SOCKS4: too long host name\\\");\\n433:           return CURLPX_LONG_HOSTNAME;\\n434:         }\\n435:         packetsize += hostnamelen;\\n436:       }\\n437:       sx->outp = socksreq;\\n438:       sx->outstanding = packetsize;\\n439:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\\n440:     }\\n441:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n442:   case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\\n443:     /* Send request */\\n444:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\\n445:                                \\\"SOCKS4 connect request\\\");\\n446:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n447:       return presult;\\n448:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n449:       /* remain in sending state */\\n450:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n451:     }\\n452:     /* done sending! */\\n453:     sx->outstanding = 8; /* receive data size */\\n454:     sx->outp = socksreq;\\n455:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\\n456: \\n457:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n458:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\\n459:     /* Receive response */\\n460:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\\n461:                                \\\"connect request ack\\\");\\n462:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n463:       return presult;\\n464:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n465:       /* remain in reading state */\\n466:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n467:     }\\n468:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\\n469:     break;\\n470:   default: /* lots of unused states in SOCKS4 */\\n471:     break;\\n472:   }\\n473: \\n474:   /*\\n475:    * Response format\\n476:    *\\n477:    *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\\n478:    *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        |\\n479:    *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\\n480:    * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4\\n481:    *\\n482:    * VN is the version of the reply code and should be 0. CD is the result\\n483:    * code with one of the following values:\\n484:    *\\n485:    * 90: request granted\\n486:    * 91: request rejected or failed\\n487:    * 92: request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to\\n488:    *     identd on the client\\n489:    * 93: request rejected because the client program and identd\\n490:    *     report different user-ids\\n491:    */\\n492: \\n493:   /* wrong version ? */\\n494:   if(socksreq[0]) {\\n495:     failf(data,\\n496:           \\\"SOCKS4 reply has wrong version, version should be 0.\\\");\\n497:     return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\\n498:   }\\n499: \\n500:   /* Result */\\n501:   switch(socksreq[1]) {\\n502:   case 90:\\n503:     infof(data, \\\"SOCKS4%s request granted.\\\", protocol4a?\\\"a\\\":\\\"\\\");\\n504:     break;\\n505:   case 91:\\n506:     failf(data,\\n507:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n508:           \\\", request rejected or failed.\\\",\\n509:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n510:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n511:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n512:     return CURLPX_REQUEST_FAILED;\\n513:   case 92:\\n514:     failf(data,\\n515:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n516:           \\\", request rejected because SOCKS server cannot connect to \\\"\\n517:           \\\"identd on the client.\\\",\\n518:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n519:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n520:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n521:     return CURLPX_IDENTD;\\n522:   case 93:\\n523:     failf(data,\\n524:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n525:           \\\", request rejected because the client program and identd \\\"\\n526:           \\\"report different user-ids.\\\",\\n527:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n528:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n529:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n530:     return CURLPX_IDENTD_DIFFER;\\n531:   default:\\n532:     failf(data,\\n533:           \\\"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. (%d)\\\"\\n534:           \\\", Unknown.\\\",\\n535:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\\n536:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\\n537:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\\n538:     return CURLPX_UNKNOWN_FAIL;\\n539:   }\\n540: \\n541:   return CURLPX_OK; /* Proxy was successful! */\\n542: }\\n543: \\n544: /*\\n545:  * This function logs in to a SOCKS5 proxy and sends the specifics to the final\\n546:  * destination server.\\n547:  */\\n548: static CURLproxycode do_SOCKS5(struct Curl_cfilter *cf,\\n549:                                struct socks_state *sx,\\n550:                                struct Curl_easy *data)\\n551: {\\n552:   /*\\n553:     According to the RFC1928, section \\\"6.  Replies\\\". /* expect two bytes */\\n643:     sx->outp = socksreq; /* store it here */\\n644:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n645:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\\n646:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\\n647:                                \\\"initial SOCKS5 response\\\");\\n648:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n649:       return presult;\\n650:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\\n651:       /* remain in reading state */\\n652:       return CURLPX_OK;\\n653:     }\\n654:     else if(socksreq[0] != 5) {\\n655:       failf(data, \\\"Received invalid version in initial SOCKS5 response.\\\");\\n656:       return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\\n657:     }\\n658:     else if(socksreq[1] == 0) {\\n659:       /* DONE! /* the length must fit in a single byte */\\n737:       if(proxy_password_len > 255) {\\n738:         failf(data, \\\"Excessive password length for proxy auth\\\");\\n739:         return CURLPX_LONG_PASSWD;\\n740:       }\\n741:       memcpy(socksreq + len, sx->proxy_password, proxy_password_len);\\n742:     }\\n743:     len += proxy_password_len;\\n744:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_SEND);\\n745:     sx->outstanding = len;\\n746:     sx->outp = socksreq;\\n747:   }\\n748:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\\n749:   case CONNECT_AUTH_SEND:\\n750:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_AUTH,\\n751:                                \\\"SOCKS5 sub-negotiation request\\\");\\n752:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\\n753:       return presult;\\n754:     else *sx,\n276:                                struct Curl_easy *data)\n277: {\n278:   struct connectdata *conn = cf->conn;\n279:   const bool protocol4a =\n280:     (conn->socks_proxy.proxytype == TRUE : FALSE;\n281:   unsigned char *socksreq = (unsigned char *)data->state.buffer;\n282:   CURLcode result;\n283:   CURLproxycode presult;\n284:   struct Curl_dns_entry *dns = NULL;\n285: \n286:   /* make sure that the buffer is at least 600 bytes */\n287:   DEBUGASSERT(READBUFFER_MIN >= 600);\n288: \n289:   switch(sx->state) {\n290:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT:\n291:     /* SOCKS4 can only do IPv4, insist! */\n292:     conn->ip_version = CURL_IPRESOLVE_V4;\n293:     if(conn->bits.httpproxy)\n294:       infof(data, \"SOCKS4%s: connecting to HTTP proxy %s port %d\",\n295:             protocol4a ? \"a\" : \"\", sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n296: \n297:     infof(data, \"SOCKS4 communication to %s:%d\",\n298:           sx->hostname, sx->remote_port);\n299: \n300:     /*\n301:      * Compose socks4 request\n302:      *\n303:      * Request format\n304:      *\n305:      *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n306:      *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        | USERID       |NULL|\n307:      *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+....+----+\n308:      * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4           variable       1\n309:      */\n310: \n311:     socksreq[0] = 4;        /* LSB */\n315: \n316:     /* DNS resolve only for SOCKS4, not SOCKS4a */\n317:     if(!protocol4a) {\n318:       enum resolve_t rc =\n319:         Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port, TRUE, &dns);\n320: \n321:       if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\n322:         return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n323:       else if(rc == CURLRESOLV_PENDING) {\n324:         sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVING);\n325:         infof(data, \"SOCKS4 non-blocking resolve of %s\", sx->hostname);\n326:         return CURLPX_OK;\n327:       }\n328:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n329:       goto CONNECT_RESOLVED;\n330:     }\n331: \n332:     /* socks4a doesn't resolve anything locally */\n333:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_INIT);\n334:     goto CONNECT_REQ_INIT;\n335: \n336:   case CONNECT_RESOLVING:\n337:     /* check if we have the name resolved by now */\n338:     dns = Curl_fetch_addr(data, sx->hostname, (int)conn->port);\n339: \n340:     if(dns) {\n341: #ifdef CURLRES_ASYNCH\n342:       data->state.async.dns = dns;\n343:       data->state.async.done = TRUE;\n344: #endif\n345:       infof(data, \"Hostname '%s' was found\", sx->hostname);\n346:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_RESOLVED);\n347:     }\n348:     else {\n349:       result = Curl_resolv_check(data, &dns);\n350:       if(!dns) {\n351:         if(result)\n352:           return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n353:         return CURLPX_OK;\n354:       }\n355:     }\n356:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n357: CONNECT_RESOLVED:\n358:   case CONNECT_RESOLVED: {\n359:     struct Curl_addrinfo *hp = NULL;\n360:     /*\n361:      * We cannot use 'hostent' as a struct that Curl_resolv() returns.  It\n362:      * returns a Curl_addrinfo pointer that may not always look the same.\n363:      */\n364:     if(dns) {\n365:       hp = dns->addr;\n366: \n367:       /* scan for the first IPv4 address */\n368:       while(hp && (hp->ai_family != AF_INET))\n369:         hp = hp->ai_next;\n370: \n371:       if(hp) {\n372:         struct sockaddr_in *saddr_in;\n373:         char buf[64];\n374:         Curl_printable_address(hp, buf, sizeof(buf));\n375: \n376:         saddr_in = (struct sockaddr_in *)(void *)hp->ai_addr;\n377:         socksreq[4] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[0];\n378:         socksreq[5] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[1];\n379:         socksreq[6] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[2];\n380:         socksreq[7] = ((unsigned char *)&saddr_in->sin_addr.s_addr)[3];\n381: \n382:         infof(data, \"SOCKS4 connect to IPv4 %s (locally resolved)\", buf);\n383: \n384:         Curl_resolv_unlock(data, dns); /* not used anymore from now on */\n385:       }\n386:       else\n387:         failf(data, \"SOCKS4 connection to %s not supported\", sx->hostname);\n388:     }\n389:     else\n390:       failf(data, \"Failed to resolve \\\"%s\\\" for SOCKS4 connect.\",\n391:             sx->hostname);\n392: \n393:     if(!hp)\n394:       return CURLPX_RESOLVE_HOST;\n395:   }\n396:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n397: CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n398:   case CONNECT_REQ_INIT:\n399:     /*\n400:      * This is currently not supporting \"Identification Protocol (RFC1413)\".\n401:      */\n402:     socksreq[8] = 0; /* ensure empty userid is NUL-terminated */\n403:     if(sx->proxy_user) {\n404:       size_t plen = strlen(sx->proxy_user);\n405:       if(plen >= (size_t)data->set.buffer_size - 8) {\n406:         failf(data, \"Too long SOCKS proxy user name, can't use\");\n407:         return CURLPX_LONG_USER;\n408:       }\n409:       /* copy the proxy name WITH trailing zero */\n410:       memcpy(socksreq + 8, sx->proxy_user, plen + 1);\n411:     }\n412: \n413:     /*\n414:      * Make connection\n415:      */\n416:     {\n417:       size_t packetsize = 9 +\n418:         strlen((char *)socksreq + 8); /* size including NUL */\n419: \n420:       /* If SOCKS4a, set special invalid IP address 0.0.0.x */\n421:       if(protocol4a) {\n422:         size_t hostnamelen = 0;\n423:         socksreq[4] = 0;\n424:         socksreq[5] = 0;\n425:         socksreq[6] = 0;\n426:         socksreq[7] = 1;\n427:         /* append hostname */\n428:         hostnamelen = strlen(sx->hostname) + 1; /* length including NUL */\n429:         if(hostnamelen <= 255)\n430:           strcpy((char *)socksreq + packetsize, sx->hostname);\n431:         else {\n432:           failf(data, \"SOCKS4: too long host name\");\n433:           return CURLPX_LONG_HOSTNAME;\n434:         }\n435:         packetsize += hostnamelen;\n436:       }\n437:       sx->outp = socksreq;\n438:       sx->outstanding = packetsize;\n439:       sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_SENDING);\n440:     }\n441:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n442:   case CONNECT_REQ_SENDING:\n443:     /* Send request */\n444:     presult = socks_state_send(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_SEND_CONNECT,\n445:                                \"SOCKS4 connect request\");\n446:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n447:       return presult;\n448:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n449:       /* remain in sending state */\n450:       return CURLPX_OK;\n451:     }\n452:     /* done sending! */\n453:     sx->outstanding = 8; /* receive data size */\n454:     sx->outp = socksreq;\n455:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_SOCKS_READ);\n456: \n457:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n458:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n459:     /* Receive response */\n460:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n461:                                \"connect request ack\");\n462:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n463:       return presult;\n464:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n465:       /* remain in reading state */\n466:       return CURLPX_OK;\n467:     }\n468:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_DONE);\n469:     break;\n470:   default: /* lots of unused states in SOCKS4 */\n471:     break;\n472:   }\n473: \n474:   /*\n475:    * Response format\n476:    *\n477:    *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n478:    *     | VN | CD | DSTPORT |      DSTIP        |\n479:    *     +----+----+----+----+----+----+----+----+\n480:    * # of bytes:  1    1      2              4\n481:    *\n482:    * VN is the version of the reply code and should be 0. (%d)\"\n508:           \", request rejected or failed.\",\n509:           socksreq[4], socksreq[5], socksreq[6], socksreq[7],\n510:           (((unsigned char)socksreq[2] << 8) | (unsigned char)socksreq[3]),\n511:           (unsigned char)socksreq[1]);\n512:     return CURLPX_REQUEST_FAILED;\n513:   case 92:\n514:     failf(data,\n515:           \"Can't complete SOCKS4 connection to %d.%d.%d.%d:%d. Replies\". /* expect two bytes */\n643:     sx->outp = socksreq; /* store it here */\n644:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n645:   case CONNECT_SOCKS_READ:\n646:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_CONNECT,\n647:                                \"initial SOCKS5 response\");\n648:     if(CURLPX_OK != presult)\n649:       return presult;\n650:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n651:       /* remain in reading state */\n652:       return CURLPX_OK;\n653:     }\n654:     else if(socksreq[0] != 5) {\n655:       failf(data, \"Received invalid version in initial SOCKS5 response.\");\n656:       return CURLPX_BAD_VERSION;\n657:     }\n658:     else if(socksreq[1] == 0) {\n659:       /* DONE! failf(data, \"Unable to negotiate SOCKS5 GSS-API context.\");\n674:         return CURLPX_GSSAPI;\n675:       }\n676:     }\n677: #endif\n678:     else {\n679:       /* error */\n680: len += proxy_password_len;\n744:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_SEND);\n745:     sx->outstanding = len;\n746:     sx->outp = socksreq;\n747:   }\n748:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n749:   case presult)\n753:       return presult;\n754:     else if(sx->outstanding) {\n755:       /* remain in sending state */\n756:       return CURLPX_OK;\n757:     }\n758:     sx->outp = socksreq;\n759:     sx->outstanding = 2;\n760:     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_AUTH_READ);\n761:     /* FALLTHROUGH */\n762:   case CONNECT_AUTH_READ:\n763:     presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data,     /* remain in reading state */\n769:       return CURLPX_OK;\n770:     }\n771:     /* ignore the first (VER) byte */\n772:     else if(socksreq[1]) { /* status */\n773:       failf(data, \"User was enum resolve_t rc = Curl_resolv(data, sx->hostname, sx->remote_port,\n785:                                       TRUE, &dns);\n786: \n787:       if(rc == CURLRESOLV_ERROR)\n788:         return The function is **REACHABLE** from external input when a user specifies a SOCKS5 proxy configuration. The function processes untrusted data from SOCKS5 proxy servers, presenting a potential attack surface for exploiting the proxy handshake implementation.\n\n## Affected Code\n\n**Function:** `do_SOCKS5()`\n**Location:** `lib/socks.c:548-1054`\n**Type:** Static function (internal)\n\n**Description:** This function implements the SOCKS5 protocol handshake as defined in RFC 1928. It manages the multi-stage negotiation between curl and a SOCKS5 proxy server, including:\n- Initial authentication method negotiation\n- Username/password authentication (if required)\n- Remote connection request to the target server\n- Response validation and error handling\n\nThe function operates as a state machine with states including:\n- `CONNECT_SOCKS_INIT`: Initialize SOCKS5 connection\n- `CONNECT_SOCKS_SEND/READ`: Exchange initial auth methods\n- `CONNECT_AUTH_INIT/SEND/READ`: Authenticate with proxy\n- `CONNECT_REQ_INIT/SEND/READ`: Send connection request to target\n- `CONNECT_DONE`: Successfully connected\n\n## Attack Path\n\n### Complete Call Chain\n\n```\nUser executes curl → easy_perform() → multi_perform() →\nmulti_runsingle() → Curl_once_resolved() →\nCurl_setup_conn() → Curl_conn_setup() →\ncf_setup_add()/Curl_cf_setup_insert_after() →\ncf_setup_create() → cf_setup_connect() [filter callback] →\nCurl_cf_socks_proxy_insert_after() →\nsocks_proxy_cf_connect() [filter callback] →\nconnect_SOCKS() → do_SOCKS5()\n```\n\n### Intermediate Functions and Their Roles\n\n1. **User Entry Point:** `curl_easy_perform()` / `curl_multi_perform()`\n   - Public API entry point when user runs curl or calls the C library\n   - Triggers the transfer initialization\n\n2. **Transfer State Machine:** `multi_runsingle()` (lib/multi.c:1868)\n   - Core state machine that orchestrates the entire transfer lifecycle\n   - Processes states: MSTATE_INIT → MSTATE_CONNECT → MSTATE_WAITRESOLVE → MSTATE_PROTOCONNECT\n   - Role: Routes control flow through DNS resolution and connection setup phases\n\n3. **Post-DNS Resolution Handler:** `Curl_once_resolved()` (lib/hostip.c:1325)\n   - Called after DNS resolution completes\n   - Invokes connection setup\n   - Role: Bridge between name resolution and connection setup\n\n4. **Connection Setup Coordinator:** `Curl_setup_conn()` (lib/url.c:3858)\n   - Checks connection configuration and prepares for data transfer\n   - Initiates filter chain setup via `Curl_conn_setup()`\n   - Role: Validates protocol handlers and initiates connection filters\n\n5. **Public Connection Setup API:** `Curl_conn_setup()` (lib/connect.c:1416)\n   - Creates and adds the connection filter chain\n   - Calls `cf_setup_add()` to install the setup filter\n   - Role: Public interface for filter chain initialization\n\n6. **Filter Chain Builder:** `cf_setup_add()` (lib/connect.c:1364) / `Curl_cf_setup_insert_after()` (lib/connect.c:1398)\n   - Creates the setup filter via `cf_setup_create()`\n   - Adds it to the filter chain\n   - Role: Instantiates the setup filter\n\n7. **Filter Creator:** `cf_setup_create()` (lib/connect.c:1332)\n   - Allocates setup filter context\n   - Returns the setup filter instance\n   - Role: Factory function for creating the setup filter\n\n8. **Setup Filter's Connect Callback:** `cf_setup_connect()` (lib/connect.c:1186)\n   - Part of the `Curl_cft_setup` filter type\n   - Checks connection type and inserts protocol-specific filters\n   - **Checks `cf->conn->bits.socksproxy` (line 1217)**\n   - **Calls `Curl_cf_socks_proxy_insert_after()` if SOCKS proxy is configured (line 1218)**\n   - Role: Orchestrates insertion of SOCKS proxy filter when needed\n\n9. **SOCKS Proxy Filter Installer:** `Curl_cf_socks_proxy_insert_after()` (lib/socks.c:1240)\n   - Creates a new SOCKS proxy filter instance\n   - Inserts it into the filter chain\n   - Role: Instantiates and installs the SOCKS filter\n\n10. **SOCKS Proxy Filter's Connect Callback:** `socks_proxy_cf_connect()` (lib/socks.c:1103)\n    - Called when the filter chain processes the connection\n    - Initializes SOCKS state machine\n    - **Calls `connect_SOCKS()` at line 1149**\n    - Role: Filter's entry point that initiates SOCKS handshake\n\n11. **SOCKS Protocol Dispatcher:** `connect_SOCKS()` (lib/socks.c:1056)\n    - Dispatches to protocol-specific handler based on proxy type\n    - Checks `conn->socks_proxy.proxytype` (lines 1064-1078)\n    - **Calls `do_SOCKS5()` for CURLPROXY_SOCKS5 and CURLPROXY_SOCKS5_HOSTNAME (lines 1065-1068)**\n    - Role: Routes to SOCKS4 or SOCKS5 handler\n\n12. **SOCKS5 Protocol Handler:** `do_SOCKS5()` (lib/socks.c:548)\n    - **Implements the SOCKS5 RFC 1928 protocol**\n    - Processes server responses at lines 654-1049\n    - Role: Core SOCKS5 state machine and protocol processor\n\n### Key Configuration Points\n\n**Where External Input Enters the System:**\n\n1. **Command-Line/API Level:** User specifies proxy via:\n   - Command line: `curl https://example.com --proxy socks5://proxy:1080`\n   - C API: `curl_easy_setopt(handle, CURLOPT_PROXY, \"socks5://proxy:1080\")`\n   - This sets: `data->set.str[STRING_PROXY]`\n\n2. **Connection Initialization (lib/url.c:1509-1549):**\n   - Function: `allocate_conn()` reads user's proxy setting\n   - Code line 1540: `conn->bits.proxy = (data->set.str[STRING_PROXY] && *data->set.str[STRING_PROXY]) ? TRUE : FALSE`\n   - Code line 1547: `conn->bits.socksproxy = (conn->bits.proxy && !conn->bits.httpproxy) ? TRUE : FALSE`\n   - **Proxy type is determined from parsed proxy URL**: `data->set.proxytype`\n\n3. **Filter Chain Setup (lib/connect.c:1217):**\n   - Setup filter checks: `if(ctx->state < CF_SETUP_CNNCT_SOCKS && cf->conn->bits.socksproxy)`\n   - **Only if user specified a SOCKS proxy does the chain insert SOCKS filter**\n\n4. **Proxy Server Responses (lib/socks.c:645-1049):**\n   - **SOCKS proxy server sends bytes received via network**\n   - `do_SOCKS5()` processes these responses in the state machine\n   - Lines 646, 763, 952: Calls to `socks_state_recv()` read proxy server's response\n   - Lines 654-691: Response validation against RFC 1928 format\n   - Lines 1005-1020: Parsing of variable-length address types\n\n## Severity Assessment\n\n### Reachability: YES - FULLY REACHABLE\n\nThe `do_SOCKS5()` function **IS reachable** from external attacker-controlled input under normal curl operation.\n\n### Attack Vector\n\n**Required User Action:**\n```bash\ncurl https://example.com --proxy socks5://attacker-controlled-proxy:1080\n```\n\nOr via C API:\n```c\ncurl_easy_setopt(handle, CURLOPT_PROXY, \"socks5://attacker-controlled-proxy:1080\");\ncurl_easy_perform(handle);\n```\n\n**Attack Prerequisites:**\n1. User must configure curl to use a SOCKS5 proxy\n2. Attacker must control or compromise the SOCKS5 proxy server\n3. Attacker configures the proxy to send malformed SOCKS5 responses\n\n### External Input Reaching the Function\n\n**Untrusted Data Path:**\n1. **Network data from proxy server** enters via socket read (lib/socks.c:241)\n   - Function: `Curl_conn_cf_recv()` reads from proxy server socket\n   - Data stored in: `socksreq` buffer (unsigned char array from `data->state.buffer`)\n   - Size: Up to `data->set.buffer_size` bytes (default 16KB, configurable)\n\n2. **Proxy server controls:**\n   - Version byte (expected 0x05) - line 654\n   - Authentication method byte - lines 658-689\n   - Address type in response - lines 1005-1020\n   - Address length field - line 1007\n   - Address data - lines 1028-1042\n\n3. **Attack-controllable fields in SOCKS5 response:**\n   ```\n   SOCKS5 Response Format:\n   +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   |VER | REP |  RSV  | ATYP | BND.ADDR | BND.PORT |\n   +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   | 1  |  1  | X'00' |  1   | Variable |    2     |\n   +----+-----+-------+------+----------+----------+\n   ```\n   - Bytes 0-3: Fixed fields\n   - Byte 3 (ATYP): Determines address type (1=IPv4, 3=domain, 4=IPv6)\n   - **Byte 4: Domain name length (if ATYP==3)** - potentially attacker-controlled\n   - Bytes 4+: Address data - **potentially unbounded read vulnerability**\n\n### Specific Vulnerability Points\n\n**Line 1007 - Address Length Parsing:**\n```c\nif(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n  /* domain name */\n  int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];  // <-- Attacker controls this byte\n  len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n}\n```\n- If ATYP is 3 (domain name), the code reads byte 4 as the domain length\n- This is **attacker-controlled** in a malicious proxy response\n- The length is used to calculate expected packet size\n\n**Line 1007-1008 - No Validation:**\n```c\nint addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\nlen = 5 + addrlen + 2;  // Could be calculated as buffer overflow size\n```\n- No validation that `addrlen` is reasonable\n- No check that `len <= remaining_buffer_size`\n- If `addrlen` is large, subsequent reads at line 1028-1042 could be vulnerable\n\n**Lines 1027-1031 - Potential Out-of-Bounds Access:**\n```c\nif(len > 10) {\n  sx->outstanding = len - 10;  // len from attacker-controlled field\n  sx->outp = &socksreq[10];\n  sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE);\n}\n```\n- Subsequent read operation at line 1041-1042 uses this length\n\n**Lines 1041-1042 - Buffer Read:**\n```c\ncase CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE:\n  presult = socks_state_recv(cf, sx, data, CURLPX_RECV_ADDRESS,\n                             \"SOCKS5 connect request address\");\n```\n- Reads `sx->outstanding` bytes (calculated from attacker field)\n- Into buffer starting at `sx->outp` (pointer calculated from `socksreq`)\n\n### Impact\n\nThe `do_SOCKS5()` function is **absolutely reachable** when a user specifies a SOCKS5 proxy. The untrusted SOCKS5 server response data reaches critical code paths with variable-length address type handling (ATYP field) that may have insufficient bounds checking.\n\n**Severity Classification: CRITICAL**\n- Reachability: Direct and intentional user action required, but straightforward\n- Attack complexity: Attacker must control proxy server (network layer attack)\n- Impact: Potential memory safety issues in address type parsing\n\n## Remediation\n\n### Input Validation Required\n\nTo securely handle SOCKS5 proxy responses:\n\n1. **Add bounds validation for domain name length (line 1007-1008):**\n   ```c\n   if(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n     /* domain name */\n     int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\n\n     // Validate: domain length must fit in remaining buffer\n     if(addrlen < 1 || addrlen > 255) {  // RFC 1928: max 255 bytes\n       failf(data, \"Invalid domain length in SOCKS5 response: %d\", addrlen);\n       return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n     }\n\n     len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n\n     // Validate: total packet size must not exceed buffer\n     if(len > READBUFFER_MIN) {  // or data->set.buffer_size\n       failf(data, \"SOCKS5 response packet size exceeds buffer\");\n       return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Add validation before reading additional data:**\n   ```c\n   if(len > 10) {\n     // Ensure we have already received at least 10 bytes\n     if(sx->outstanding <= 0) {\n       failf(data, \"Invalid SOCKS5 response state\");\n       return CURLPX_RECV_REQACK;\n     }\n\n     sx->outstanding = len - 10;\n\n     // Validate: don't read more than buffer can hold\n     if(sx->outstanding > READBUFFER_MIN - 10) {\n       failf(data, \"SOCKS5 response would overflow buffer\");\n       return CURLPX_RECV_REQACK;\n     }\n\n     sx->outp = &socksreq[10];\n     sxstate(sx, data, CONNECT_REQ_READ_MORE);\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Add consistent bounds checking for IPv6 responses (line 1010-1012):**\n   ```c\n   else if(socksreq[3] == 4) {\n     /* IPv6 - fixed size */\n     len = 4 + 16 + 2;\n     // IPv6 addresses are fixed 16 bytes, safe\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Strict validation of ATYP field:**\n   ```c\n   if(socksreq[3] != 1 && socksreq[3] != 3 && socksreq[3] != 4) {\n     failf(data, \"SOCKS5 reply has unknown address type: %d\", socksreq[3]);\n     return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n   }\n   ```\n\n### Summary\n\n- **Function is REACHABLE**: Direct user action (--proxy socks5://) triggers the code path\n- **External Input Path**: SOCKS5 proxy server responses enter via network sockets\n- **Vulnerability Type**: Potential integer overflow or buffer bounds violation in variable-length address type parsing\n- **Recommended Action**: Add RFC 1928 compliance validation for domain name length and total packet size before buffer operations\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1370,"cache_read_input_tokens":73863,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1370},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a9aeca5e-c218-4078-97b1-2e9f9f202822","uuid":"e69e1e8a-1f1e-4248-8726-0c3ecd7418de"}

The untrusted SOCKS5 server response data reaches critical code paths with variable-length address type handling (ATYP field) that may have insufficient bounds checking.\n\n**Severity Classification: CRITICAL**\n- Reachability: Direct and intentional user action required, but straightforward\n- Attack complexity: Attacker must control proxy server (network layer attack)\n- Impact: Potential memory safety issues in address type parsing\n\n## Remediation\n\n### Input Validation Required\n\nTo securely handle SOCKS5 proxy responses:\n\n1. **Add bounds validation for domain name length (line 1007-1008):**\n   ```c\n   if(socksreq[3] == 3) {\n     /* domain name */\n     int addrlen = (int) socksreq[4];\n\n     // Validate: domain length must fit in remaining buffer\n     if(addrlen < 1 || addrlen > 255) {  // RFC 1928: max 255 bytes\n       failf(data, \"Invalid domain length in SOCKS5 response: %d\", addrlen);\n       return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n     }\n\n     len = 5 + addrlen + 2;\n\n     // Validate: total packet size must not exceed buffer\n     if(len > READBUFFER_MIN) {  // or data->set.buffer_size\n       failf(data, \"SOCKS5 response packet size exceeds buffer\");\n       return CURLPX_BAD_ADDRESS_TYPE;\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Add validation before reading additional data:**\n   ```c\n   if(len > 10) {\n     // Ensure we have already received at least 10 bytes\n     if(sx->outstanding <= 0) {\n       failf(data, \"Invalid SOCKS5 response state\");\n       return CURLPX_RECV_REQACK;\n     }\n\n     sx->outstanding = len -
